Sino-French-Vietnamese Agreement 118

Delay in Signing Issue

Chinese Commissioner Chu Minyi Expresses His Opinion

Overseas Chinese Request Accepted

Guowen News Agency Singapore Correspondence: Since the Sino-Vietnamese old agreement was announced to be abolished and the new agreement has been delayed in signing, the Vietnamese French government has treated overseas Chinese as people from non-treaty countries, imposing exorbitant taxes and levies, doing everything possible to suppress them. The arbitrary increase in tariffs has caused the overseas Chinese business situation to decline, and domestically produced goods cannot be imported and sold due to the increased tax rate and excessive burden. Overseas Chinese merchants have suffered greatly. Recently, the French government issued regulations restricting overseas Chinese merchants. From May 1st of this year, all stores in Vietnam with an annual license tax of more than 500 yuan (in addition to the regular tax, there will be an additional tax of more than 40%) must use French bookkeeping. The Chinese General Chamber of Commerce in Cochinchina has repeatedly requested that this be changed, but the French Resident Superior in Vietnam, citing that the Sino-Vietnamese new agreement has not yet been concluded, will implement this forcibly. Overseas Chinese are experiencing great pain in politics and commerce due to the inequality of their international status and the absence of a Chinese consulate in Vietnam. There is no way to appeal. This time, when Chinese Commissioner Dr. Chu Minyi visited Vietnam, the overseas Chinese earnestly requested his intervention on this important issue and asked him to convey their request to Gao Lu, the Chinese Minister to France, for direct negotiations with the French government to fight for their rights based on reason. At the same time, they hoped that the Sino-Vietnamese new agreement would be signed as soon as possible to alleviate the suffering of the overseas Chinese. The doctor has agreed to their request and, in addition to formally presenting the document to Minister Gao, has also instructed Tang, the Chinese Consul General in Singapore, to send a telegram to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to investigate and handle the matter. Dr. Chu's views on the Sino-Vietnamese new agreement are briefly described below: Overseas Chinese engage in business overseas, living frugally and enduring hardship. They are repeatedly humiliated by the authorities in their countries of residence due to the inequality of their international status. Their pain is almost indescribable. The enthusiasm of the overseas Chinese for loving their country and donating funds is evident in their past achievements and is clear for all to see. The Sino-Vietnamese old agreement has already been abolished, but the new agreement has not yet been signed. During this transitional period, the losses have been significant, and the diplomatic authorities are difficult to excuse. The abolition of unequal treaties has instead lost its protection. I (the doctor referring to himself), as a consultant to the Treaty Committee of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, should bear the responsibility. The other day, I met Pasgier, the Governor of Cochinchina, Knautheimer, the Governor of Cochinchina, and Chatodemis, and expressed my views on this important issue. I still hope that you will show temporary tolerance. The Chinese and French authorities will definitely have a solution in the near future. The presentation of the Chinese General Chamber of Commerce in Cochinchina is recorded below: The presentation is for a request. It should be noted that the use of Western commercial bookkeeping is stipulated in the Sino-Vietnamese old treaty, and overseas Chinese in Vietnam are never required to implement it. Now, the Vietnamese French government has issued an order to implement Western commercial bookkeeping in stores owned by Chinese merchants in Vietnam with a regular tax of more than 500 yuan from May 1st of this year. The overseas Chinese in Vietnam are terrified. They are currently trying to request that the case be canceled, but it is not known whether they will be able to achieve this goal. Back in 1925, the Vietnamese French government proposed that Chinese businesses use Western bookkeeping. At the time, Mr. Ye Boxing, the former chairman of the association, was in office. For this matter, Mr. Ye convened several meetings of Chinese business directors at the association. Everyone believed that the matter was difficult to implement, and Mr. Ye was publicly elected to present a request to the Governor of Cochinchina to form a committee to review the matter. The committee consisted of the chairman of the Western Chamber of Commerce, a first-class advisor appointed by the Vietnamese French government, the secretary of the Mayor of Dike, and the former manager of the Saigon Asia Foreign Company. The committee held two meetings on October 30th and November 6th, 1925. Mr. Ye reported to the committee the situation that Chinese people had difficulty implementing Western bookkeeping. The committee acknowledged that the report was true. The Vietnamese French government was concerned that there might be errors or unclear points in the Chinese commercial accounts. Mr. Ye proposed that the association hire two auditors, and the government could entrust the association to review the Chinese accounts if they found them unclear. Chinese people would not have to use Western bookkeeping. Thus, the case of Chinese people using Western bookkeeping was presented by the committee to the Vietnamese French government for temporary suspension of implementation. In 1928, the association hired two auditors and reported their names to the Saigon Commercial Court for record. They subsequently received a reply approving this. The president of the court also summoned five accounting officials in Saigon to inquire whether any malpractices had been found in the Chinese commercial accounts they had handled. They replied that no fraudulent activities had ever been found in the accounts of large Chinese businesses with license taxes. As for the occasional messy accounts, they belonged to stores with license taxes of 7th or 8th class or lower, due to the merchants' lack of knowledge. It can be seen that the malpractice does not arise from the use of Chinese writing. The court president also believed this to be the real situation. Now, the Vietnamese French government has suddenly overturned the previous case. Cai Bojiu negotiated with the Governor of Cochinchina on the 2nd of this month, requesting that the case of Chinese people implementing Western commercial bookkeeping be canceled. However, the Governor cited that our government has repeatedly delayed signing the Sino-Vietnamese new agreement, causing Chinese people residing here to be treated as people from non-treaty countries. He also said that Western commercial bookkeeping is not only required for foreigners. In this way, the Vietnamese government is determined to implement the case of Western commercial bookkeeping, which greatly hinders the commerce of our overseas Chinese. Overseas Chinese in Vietnam are very opposed to this. Please negotiate with the French government nearby to quickly cancel the case of Chinese people implementing Western commercial bookkeeping in Vietnam, so as to alleviate the difficulties of the overseas Chinese. All overseas Chinese will be very grateful for this great virtue. Respectfully presented to Gao, the Minister of the Republic of China in France. Cai Bojiu, Chairman of the Chinese General Chamber of Commerce in Cochinchina.

Information for Chinese Citizens Traveling to Siam 119

Since China and Siam have not yet signed a treaty of commerce, Chinese citizens traveling to Siam are naturally governed by the laws of the place where they reside. However, the Siamese government has long prohibited private groups and charitable organizations from various countries from sending personnel to Siam to solicit donations from overseas Chinese. The government has also repeatedly expressed dissatisfaction with important figures from various countries coming to Siam to promote their countries' politics. The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce received a letter from the local General Chamber of Commerce yesterday, stating that in the future, if any personnel are sent to Siam to solicit donations or engage in propaganda, they should first submit a request to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for verification of international procedures and inform the Siamese government. They should also obtain a valid passport to enter Siam to avoid being detained and to ensure safe travel.

According to news from the U.S. Commercial Commissioner's Office in this city, the Sixth International Road Congress is scheduled to be held in Washington, D.C. in October of this year. Road engineers and road officials from various countries will attend. The scope of discussion is quite extensive, including road administration reports on the construction and maintenance of various types of roads, the performance of using cement bricks and stones to build road surfaces, the latest methods of using asphalt and bitumen, the construction of highways in remote areas, and the most important methods of fundraising for road construction. In addition, transportation issues, urban traffic systems, traffic signal designs, and parking problems will each occupy a portion of the agenda. Therefore, for those seeking road construction and transportation development, this congress offers an excellent opportunity for reference. Furthermore, attending representatives and visitors can enjoy various benefits, such as discounted train tickets for representatives and their families on U.S. railways, and a 25% discount on accommodation at Washington D.C. hotels. In addition, during the week of the congress, the latest road construction machinery will be displayed at the Washington D.C. City Hall, and practical demonstrations will be held regularly at East Potomac Park for reference. After the congress, the American Automobile Association will organize tours, divided into three itineraries of four, six, and sixteen days, touring the famous cities and scenic spots of the United States. Families of the S.S. Xin Da Ming Hold a Meeting 126

Setting Ten Thousand Yuan as the Minimum Standard

Denying the Social Bureau's Overstepping of Authority

The S.S. Xin Da Ming of the former Datong Xieji Steamship Company was unjustifiably sunk by the Japanese merchant Sato Shokai's Atsuta No. 2 Maru in February of the 17th year of the Republic of China in the Dongxingang area of Waisha, Chongming, causing 365 passenger and crew members to perish (evidence has been verified). The loss of cargo was estimated at several hundred thousand. The Chinese and Japanese sides had long invited impartial individuals to form an arbitration committee, which determined that the Japanese side should be liable for 265,000 in compensation for the loss of cargo. Later, because the Japanese side delayed payment, after repeated negotiations, Datong Company suddenly agreed to reduce the compensation to 180,000 in cash to resolve the matter. However, the diplomatic authorities considered the compensation for loss of life to be important, concerning national rights and the lives of the people, and could not be arbitrated, so it was necessary to make formal representations to the Japanese side. However, since handling the negotiations, the Japanese side has only acknowledged 25,000 Japanese yen. All the families believe that 25,000 Japanese yen, calculated at the current market rate, is equivalent to 40,000 national currency, with each family receiving only about 100 yuan. If this is acknowledged, the lives of Chinese people will have a fixed price. Future diplomacy will use this as an example, and our country's ships can be arbitrarily sunk to destroy our shipping rights. Therefore, everyone denies this and demands that the minimum amount be 1,000 yuan per person. However, for the sake of forbearance, if the Japanese side is sincere in resolving the matter, it will be reduced to a standard of 100,000 yuan. The Japanese side has been ignoring this ever since Lawyer Wu Kaisheng represented the families last year, and more than half a year has passed. The Japanese side is still deliberately delaying, hoping to end the matter without resolution. Since Lawyer Wu went abroad, the case has been handled by Lawyers Wu Chengzi, Chen Zemin, and Gao Shuo. However, there is still no increased hope. Unexpectedly, the Social Bureau recently approved the Haiyuan Gonghui's (Seamen's Union's) request to negotiate labor-capital issues with Yang Zaitian of Datong Company. Yang Zaitian specially appointed Ma Xishen and Gao Shuo as representatives to resolve the labor-capital dispute. It was unexpectedly resolved with the Japanese side agreeing to 25,000 Japanese yen as the standard for resolving the case, and there was a distinction between crew members and passengers, with the compensation being divided into a 40-60 split. All the families were greatly shocked upon hearing the news. They went to Lawyer Wu's office for several days, requesting to declare to the Social Bureau that they did not recognize the resolution of the case. Lawyer Wu considered the case to be important and discussed it with Lawyers Chen and Gao. At 4:00 PM yesterday, a representative meeting was convened for all the families at Lawyer Wu's office on Nanjing Road. More than 50 people attended, and the general representative, Pei Jiesan, was elected as the chairman to report on the progress of the situation (see previous summary). Next, each family expressed their opinions, and the resolutions were as follows: (1) This case concerns diplomacy and law, not a labor-capital dispute. The handling and resolution by the Social Bureau is considered inappropriate, and all the families unanimously deny it and request the representative lawyers in this case to protest. (2) Lawyer Gao Shuo, who represented the case, should be asked to state his position on signing the case. (3) The Japanese side's compensation of 25,000 Japanese yen is denied, and based on the previous agreement, the minimum amount is 100,000 yuan. In the future, the money received should be distributed equally between passengers and crew members. The special treatment of crew members should be the responsibility of the shipowner and should not be a condition for life compensation. (4) Send a letter to Yang Zaitian, declaring that the minimum amount of compensation for the families is 100,000 yuan. If a private settlement is made and 40,000 yuan is received from the Japanese side, Mr. Yang should be responsible for 100,000 yuan. (5) The recent handling of the situation and the Social Bureau's handling of labor-capital issues that encroached on the scope of diplomatic law should be reported to the National Government's Ministry of Foreign Affairs, requesting that serious representations be made to the Japanese side to prevent other agencies from overstepping their authority, so as to emphasize national rights and the lives of the people. The above resolutions were unanimously approved and passed. The meeting adjourned at 7:00 PM.

British and Japanese Merchants Compete for Northern Shipping Rights 128

Rushing to Build Ships to Prepare for Expansion

After our country's claim to recover shipping rights, Japanese shipping companies immediately began to add ships and increase the frequency of services on various routes along the coast of our country. British shipping companies are not willing to be outdone and are doing their best to compete for shipping rights along the coast of China. The competition is currently intensifying in the northern route. What has been learned recently is reported as follows:

Japanese Ships Increase Freight Rates to Tianjin Direct ships from Japan to Tianjin, operated by Osaka and Nippon Yusen Kaisha (NYK), each operate four ships. In addition, NYK also operates four ships to Yingkou and Andong, in order to facilitate the direct transportation of Japanese goods to northern China. Recently, citing the low silver price and increased ship operating expenses, NYK has decided to implement a price increase for freight rates on the Tianjin route, and it is said that it has been agreed to increase the original rate by 30%. At the same time, it is also planned to increase the freight rates for goods shipped from Japan to Qingdao by 30%. It is said that this new freight rate is being drafted.

British Merchants Add New Ships to Northern Routes The British merchant company Butterfield & Swire has the most ships in this city and is also the most aggressive in its business operations. On the northern route, the company has regular ships, such as the Tongzhou, Shuntian, and Fengtian, which depart every three days. Since the Dalian Company added Shanghai-Tianjin liner services last winter, Butterfield & Swire has planned to build two fast ships with strong speed to compete with Japanese merchants in North China shipping. The two ships are being built at the company's own shipyard in Hong Kong, and their speed and cargo capacity are larger than those of the Tongzhou and others. It is said that one ship will be completed this year. Jardine Matheson & Co. is also adding a new ship to the northern route, using an oil engine and paying great attention to passenger capacity. It can also be completed this year.

Dalian's New Ship to be Completed Soon The Dalian Steamship Company's third new ship, the Changchun Maru, is being built by the Mitsubishi Shipyard in Kobe, and is specially designed to develop cargo and passenger connections between southern Manchuria and Shanghai. The cost is 2 million Japanese yen, the net tonnage is 3,950 tons, and there are 50 first-class cabins, 27 second-class cabins, and 50 third-class cabins. The fourth-class can carry more than 300 people. The hull of the ship has already been built. The company received a telegram from the head office stating that the new ship Changchun Maru is scheduled to arrive in Shanghai for operation at the end of August. At the same time, a new route will be opened between Guangzhou and Tianjin.

New Yizhou Opens a Shipping Port The China-Korea liner of the Joseon Steamship Company operates between Shanghai, Busan, Incheon, and Zhenmupu. Now, due to goods being loaded from New Yizhou to Shanghai, the company has agreed to open a shipping port in New Yizhou from the export ship of May 13th at the request of the local merchants. Yesterday, it sent a telegram to Shanghai, ordering the Shanghai office to collect export goods to New Yizhou from today.

Xin Feng Damaged in Collision and Comes to Shanghai for Repairs 129

The Fault Lies Entirely with the Lighter

Tai Shun Temporarily Takes Over Tianjin Route

The S.S. Xin Feng of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company was damaged in the bow by an iron lighter inside the Dagukou during its voyage from Tianjin to Shanghai. This matter has been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday, the ship arrived in Shanghai from northern China. Because the hull was damaged, it must be taken out of service for repairs. The details of the collision are recorded below:

Bow Damaged The S.S. Xin Feng departed from Zizhu Lin last Friday. While traveling near the Caijia Gang River surface of Dagukou, two iron lighters of the Dagukou Lighter Company, fully loaded with gasoline, passed by, towed by a small tugboat into the Baihe River. The S.S. Xin Feng was traveling according to the navigation channel, and the two iron lighters coming head-on, the last one with the tow cable broken, the hull became horizontal, temporarily unable to stop and crashed into the bow of the S.S. Xin Feng. The S.S. Xin Feng tried to avoid, but it was too late, causing a large hole to be struck in the left bow compartment. Seawater immediately entered the ship. Fortunately, it was a water compartment, so the goods were not damaged. But the ship could no longer go to sea, and immediately returned to Tanggu for repairs.

Lighter Damaged The offending iron lighter was huge, with a capacity of 500 tons, and heavily loaded, so the impact force was great. The head of the lighter was also destroyed on the spot. The lighter immediately sank horizontally in the river, blocking the channel. Both inbound and outbound ships were unable to pass. Later, after being towed by a tugboat, the S.S. Xin Feng was requested to push the sunken iron lighter from behind to the beach to run aground. The boatmen in the lighter all escaped to the tugboat, and most of the gasoline it was carrying was lost. Tai Shun Takes Over The hole in the Xin Feng caused by the collision is about three feet. After the ship arrived at the Tanggu Wharf and docked for two days, wooden boards were temporarily used to cover the hole. An on-site investigation was conducted with the Dagukou Lighter Company to determine the truth of the accident. As a result, the lighter side admitted its mistake, and the Xin Feng's damage and losses must be borne by the lighter company. Yesterday, the ship arrived in Shanghai with passengers and cargo safe. Because the damage needs major repairs urgently, the bureau decided to dispatch the Tai Shun to temporarily take over the route. The Xin Feng can enter the dock today.

Anti-Drug Association 132

Preparing to Commemorate Lin Zexu

June 3rd is the 91st anniversary of the burning of British merchants' opium by Lin Wenzhong Gong, the pioneer of anti-drug efforts in our country. Last year, on the 90th anniversary, the National Government ordered all provinces, cities, and counties to hold commemorations on this day to show commendation. The Chinese National Anti-Drug Association believes that the commemoration of the public should be expanded this year, so the association has prepared a general outline of commemoration methods and notified anti-drug organizations in various places to jointly prepare and hold the commemoration on time with local sympathetic organizations and party and government agencies. The notification methods are excerpted as follows: (1) Notification, respectfully opening, tracing back to the late Ming and early Qing dynasties, foreign opium was sold well in our country, and the whole country was in a state of darkness. The good bodies of the people were completely destroyed, and the society and the country suffered great losses. The opium-producing countries of the great powers did their best to poison China in order to achieve their aggressive ambitions. Fortunately, Lin Gong Zexu witnessed the great difficulties and deeply knew that opium was enough to destroy the country and destroy the body. He took decisive measures to burn British merchants' opium to show his determination to ban it. Unfortunately, due to the lack of organization in the Qing government and the abandonment of military preparations, it was unable to fight. In addition, the officials in the court and the public were deeply poisoned, thinking that Lin Gong's actions were illegal and instead paid compensation to Britain and begged for peace, creating the beginning of unequal treaties and plunging our country into a state of no return. Now, it has been 91 years since Lin Gong burned opium. Last year, the National Government ordered commendation and held commemorations throughout the country to commemorate the past sages and encourage the future struggle. June 3rd of this year is the day of commemoration. All our anti-drug organizations should hold commemorations on this day to show respect and encourage them. The corresponding letter, please unite with local party and government agencies and Qing organizations to prepare properly in advance and hold it on time. The future of anti-drug efforts is deeply reliant on it. (2) Methods: (1) Hold a memorial meeting, (2) Publish a commemorative special issue, (3) Hold a public lecture, (4) Hold a parade and propaganda, (5) Art propaganda, (6) Burn drugs, (7) Hold an anti-drug oath, (8) Post slogans widely, (9) Sell anti-drug monthly magazines.

Mediation of Pharmacy Labor Dispute 134

Both Labor and Capital Sides Send Representatives to the Capital

Following the labor dispute in the pharmaceutical industry arising from the issue of accommodating unemployed workers, the central government dispatched Shi Weihuan, Secretary of the Training Department, to Shanghai to investigate. Subsequently, a regular meeting decided on six measures to resolve the case and revised the third article, handing them over to the Shanghai Municipal Party Department and the Municipal Government for handling. After receiving the second order from the central government, the Municipal Party Department and the Municipal Government consulted and resolved five measures, instructing the labor side to resume work on April 24th and limiting the capital side to employing 70 unemployed workers within three days. The various situations have been repeatedly reported in the previous newspaper, but the capital side has delayed fulfilling its obligations and has sent a large number of representatives to petition the central government. Upon hearing this, the labor side also sent representatives to the capital to state everything and accuse the capital side of disobeying the central government's orders, requesting that an order be issued for their arrest. The central government then ordered the Shanghai Municipal Party Department and the Municipal Government to strictly enforce the orders. Yesterday afternoon, the representatives of the capital side returned to Shanghai from the capital. The labor side specially waited at the North Railway Station, requesting the Public Security Bureau to detain one of the representatives, Feng Jinpu. The other two escaped upon hearing the news. It is said that Feng will be transferred to the Municipal Government today.

Local News II

The Case of Burying One's Only Son Alive 136

The Inside Story Revealed

Genbao Has Already Fled

Caidi Has Also Gone Missing

Adultery Reveals Springtime

Murder for Property

Mao Da, the 13-year-old only son of Guan Liukun, a villager at No. 45 Yangjiajing Guannong, Tanzikou, Zhabei, was suddenly buried alive and killed the other day. This was discovered by Guan's sister, Hou Guan, while she was cutting grass in the field. At the same time, all three sons of Hou Guan have disappeared, giving rise to great suspicion. Details were reported in yesterday's newspaper. However, no one knew exactly why Guan's three sons committed such a heinous act. Some said that Guan Liukun had reprimanded his nephew severely, causing him to harbor resentment, plot murder, and vent his anger. But it is unlikely that a person would be put to death for such a trivial matter. After a day of investigation by the reporter, the truth has come out. There is a secret affair involved, which is reported as follows:

Love for Sons, Not Daughters Guan Liukun's first wife died of illness many years ago. She gave birth to a daughter named Caidi, who is now 19 years old and has a good appearance. She has been helping her father farm at home. Later, Guan remarried Chen, who gave birth to a son, Mao Da, who was buried alive. He is 13 years old this year. After Guan had a son, he was overjoyed that the family line could be continued. He raised him carefully and cultivated him with enthusiasm. He originally planned to recruit a son-in-law, but now he sent his daughter to work in a yarn factory and chose another name for her. Caidi was out of favor, filled with resentment, and had no opportunity to vent it.

Genbao Gambles Hou Guan, who lives in the Hou family's house, is Guan's second sister and has been a widow for many years. She has three sons: Ai Bi, A Er, and the youngest Genbao. Ai Bi and A Er help their mother with farm work and are considered stable, but Genbao is lazy and likes to gamble. Because he lives not far from Guannong, he often goes to his uncle's house to chat. Guan treats him very well, but he always scolds him for irregular behavior.

Springtime Revealed When Caidi had not yet entered the factory to work, she and Genbao would play with each other whenever Genbao came home. Their intimacy was beyond the ordinary. At first, they were just childhood sweethearts, but as they grew older, their feelings were awakened. Over time, they had an affair. Guan Liukun left early and returned late, very busy, and Guan's wife suffered from madness and sat in the bedroom all day, unaware of their obscene behavior. Unexpectedly, good things are often frustrated. Last month, when Genbao and Caidi were having a secret meeting, Mao Da happened to return home from school and accidentally saw them, revealing the hidden affair. Genbao was afraid of being exposed, so he threatened Mao Da and told him to keep it a secret, or he would take his life. Mao Da was very afraid and did not announce it.

Strike First Since Genbao had an affair with Caidi, he wanted to silence Mao Da and treat him kindly. But lately, Genbao had been doing this for a long time and treated it as nothing. Sometimes he even scolded or beat him. Mao Da was extremely angry and said, "I will tell your affairs to my father!" Genbao was very frightened when he heard this and discussed it with his two brothers. They all said that it was better to strike first, and they thought that after killing Mao Da, they could seize his property. So a tragedy was created.

Tragedy of Burial Alive At about 5:00 PM on the 6th, Genbao and his two brothers went to a field next to the Yangjiajing tomb and dug a hole about five feet deep and three feet wide. Genbao lured Mao Da out to play and passed by the pre-dug hole, turned him upside down and inserted him into it, and covered him with mud. He died in an instant.

Daughter Also Missing The other day, Hou Guan went to the field to cut grass and saw a piece of land that had been dug by someone. She took a shovel and dug it up, revealing the body and reporting it to Guan. At first, she did not know who the murderer was, but when Genbao and others fled, she suspected them. Unexpectedly, Caidi also suddenly disappeared yesterday, so the case became clear. The Fourth District Office is now ordering the police to strictly apprehend them and bring them to justice. Yesterday morning, the prosecutor appointed by the Special District District Court came to examine the body and ordered the family to take it away for burial after verifying that it was buried alive before death.

Champagne Ticket Winner 137

Jockey Harry Lewis Suspended

The Da Wan Bao reports: This year's Shanghai horse racing's Champagne Sweepstakes will be an event that Shanghai residents will likely remember for a long time. At the very least, thirty-five detectives from the Shanghai Municipal Police will have a permanent memento, as they won the second prize of 64,000 yuan in the A-category Champagne Sweepstakes. This amounts to approximately 1,900 yuan per person. They pooled their money to buy the ticket on April 1st, which Westerners call April Fool's Day. Unexpectedly, it turned into a lucky day. Therefore, these detectives will hold a celebration banquet tomorrow (the 9th). One of them, Western Detective Quail, has double the joy, as he not only owns shares in the second prize but also won the third prize of 32,000 yuan solely. As for the first prize, half of it was won by a Japanese merchant from a small shop on Rue du Consulat, totaling over 120,000 yuan. In addition, two Westerners from the J. L. Morrison & Co. are also winners of this prize. The person who purchased the ticket on their behalf was veterinarian Edward Hagger. The first prize for the B-category Champagne Sweepstakes was won by a Western merchant from Kobe, a lucky individual who has frequently won the Shanghai horse racing Champagne Sweepstakes. The jockey who suffered the greatest loss in this race was Harry Lewis. He is one of the best jockeys in China and was originally scheduled to ride the most promising horse, "Breezy Pea." However, before the final race, he asked Edward Hagger to purchase a one-tenth share of the horse's Champagne ticket. Hagger reported this to the Western stewards of the Shanghai Race Club, who immediately suspended Lewis indefinitely. Another jockey was assigned to replace him. Subsequently, the horse won first place. However, the jockey stated that the entire matter was a misunderstanding and that sharing Champagne ticket winnings is a common practice in the horse racing circle. He added that he was not at all concerned about not being able to purchase a share of the Champagne ticket, but was deeply saddened by not being able to show his skills and win the race. Last night, there were rumors that the jockey intended to file a lawsuit, but this morning (the 8th), it was claimed that this story was fabricated. He is currently seeking reinstatement. It is said that he has been a jockey for ten years and has a spotless record.

Public Concession 138

Rickshaw Licenses Difficult to Add

Municipal Council Has Given Formal Reply

Chen Shiguang, Director of the Diplomatic Affairs Office in Shanghai, previously received instructions from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to urgently negotiate with the British Municipal Council regarding the petition from rickshaw merchant Zheng Limin to add 5,161 rickshaw licenses to help the 100,000 unemployed workers in Shanghai. Director Chen exchanged views informally with Edwardes, Secretary-General of the Municipal Council, who verbally indicated that a written reply would be given only after a thorough discussion by a special committee. Director Chen had already submitted a report to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for review. Director Chen received a written reply from Edwardes yesterday, stating that the increase or decrease of rickshaws in the Public Concession must be a natural trend based on the number of motor vehicles and the smoothness of traffic. With motor vehicles and trams crowding the roads, and the existing 10,000 rickshaws often having empty vehicles vying for passengers on the streets, it would be difficult to reissue the 5,161 rickshaw licenses that were withdrawn in 1924, as this would obstruct traffic. The Council shares the concern for relieving unemployed rickshaw pullers, but rickshaw pullers must be familiar with the Municipal Council's traffic regulations, and not just anyone can pull a rickshaw, with the primary goal of ensuring the safety of passengers. After a meeting of the special committee, it was unanimously agreed that, under the current circumstances, not only can rickshaw licenses not be added, but the future development of traffic in the concession may lead to a reduction of rickshaws to 5,000 by 1936. Therefore, pulling a rickshaw cannot be a temporary occupation for unemployed workers. For the above reasons, it is difficult to add licenses. It is reported that Director Chen has already reported back to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs.

Fao Shing Steamer 139

Passenger Jumps Overboard

Passenger Jumps Overboard at Sanjia Shoal

Searched the Sea for One Hour Without Success

The Jardine Matheson shipping company's northern route Faoshing steamer, southbound from Tianjin, arrived at Sanjia Shoal outside Wusong Port at 2 PM yesterday when a passenger of unknown name suddenly jumped overboard. Upon hearing the news, the ship's captain immediately ordered the ship to stop and lower the boat to search the sea. After searching for about an hour without finding any trace, the ship continued its voyage to Shanghai. According to passengers on the ship, the person who jumped overboard was about fifty years old, and his name was unknown. The reason for jumping overboard is also unclear. It was also said that the Faoshing steamer went off course by forty nautical miles in the Black Ocean, and the ship was delayed for one hour off the coast due to someone jumping overboard. As a result, the ship did not arrive at the port until 6 PM yesterday, five hours late.

Life Problems 140

Young Woman Hangs Herself

Wife Unwilling to Live as Guests in Another's Home

Good Couple Ends Poorly

A young woman from Haizhou, Ji Yin, had a slight disagreement with her husband and suddenly hanged herself at home the evening before last. The details are reported as follows:

A Loving Couple Ji Xiaoshunzi, 26 years old, from Hefei, Anhui, rented a room at No. 21 Yude Lane, Dongchang Road, Pudong. He works as a laborer at the British American Tobacco factory in Lujiazui, earning 15 yuan a month. His wife, Yin, named Lindi, is from Haizhou, 29 years old, and quite beautiful. They married in April last year. Yin used to work at the Nichihua Cotton Mill, but stopped working due to illness. They have no children. The couple's relationship was usually quite good.

Life Problems Recently, Ji found the cost of living quite high and his income insufficient to make ends meet. Therefore, he went to his older brother, Xiaowuzi's home, to discuss ways to save expenses. His brother and sister-in-law both advised Xiaoshunzi to pay for his meals at their home, so he would not have to live alone and save money. Xiaoshunzi was pleased to hear this and went home to discuss it with his wife. Unexpectedly, Yin strongly opposed it. Ji was very upset when he saw his wife reject this arrangement, and a quarrel broke out between them. From then on, Ji ate at his sister-in-law's house every day, while Yin borrowed food from her mother's home nearby because she had no money for food. Recently, they had another conflict over this issue, and a tragedy suddenly occurred.

Crying Over Her Corpse Yin did not agree with her husband's opinion, which angered him. Overwhelmed with anger, she suddenly entered the room and hanged herself from a beam at 5 PM the day before last, while her husband was still at work. After a while, a female landlord returned home and found the bedroom door tightly closed. Suspecting something was wrong, she tried to push it open but could not. She immediately called neighbors to move the door, and they saw Yin hanging from the beam. They were panicked and immediately rushed to inform her mother and brother. They took Yin down, but she was already dead. There was no way to save her. Soon after, Xiaoshunzi also returned from work and was distraught to see the tragedy. He held his wife's body and cried loudly. He was then taken to the Third District Police Station for questioning.

Mother's Family Quarrel After Yin's death, her mother, Yin Xu, and her brother, Yin Bukang, insisted that Xiaoshunzi abused her to death and claimed that they wanted to file a lawsuit in court to seek justice. Xiaoshunzi had just returned from the Third District when he was grabbed and argued with. Later, Xiaoshunzi's older brother, Xiaowuzi, came forward to mediate, agreeing to bury the deceased with generous funds and hire a Taoist priest to perform a service for her soul. The deceased's family then had no objection and agreed to request the court to waive the autopsy yesterday. Unexpectedly, yesterday morning, Xiaoshunzi bought a coffin without consulting his wife's family. His mother-in-law, Xu, believed that the coffin material was not good and insisted on replacing it, but she failed. Negotiations broke down again overnight.

Beating the Local Constable Yesterday morning, Xie Along, the local constable of the twenty-fourth ward and twenty-fourth district, went to investigate, intending to report to the local court for an autopsy. Unexpectedly, when he arrived at the scene, the deceased's family did not recognize him as the local constable and ordered him not to make a public announcement. Xie debated with them, which resulted in him being punched twice by the family. Xie believed that it was unreasonable for him to be beaten for no reason, and he had never heard of a corpse's family beating a local constable, so he went to the Third District to report the incident. The district sent a police officer to take the deceased's brother, Bukang, to the district and send him to the local court for questioning. The matter was soon resolved peacefully.

Autopsy Today At the same time, the local constable filed a request for the court to send someone across the river to perform an autopsy. The court originally scheduled to send a prosecutor and an inspector to the scene this afternoon, but because it was too late, it was changed to 9 AM today. Therefore, the body was not yet placed in the coffin last night.

Suicide Due to Life's Pressures 141

Chen Liang, also known as Hongfu, was a 23-year-old native of Ningxian, Zhejiang. He worked at the Yufeng Lumberyard at the north end of Xijiaxing Road Bridge on Dixiwei Road. He married Xu, who is now 19 years old, and they rented a house together at No. 8 Yuanchang Road, Hujiamu Bridge. Chen Liang earned a monthly salary of eight yuan, which was used to support the family, but he often worried that it was not enough. Xu also worked as a servant to supplement their income. At 3 PM the day before last, Chen left the store alone. He did not return home that evening and stayed overnight at the Xinxin Hotel on Xin Jia Road, Dixiwei Road. At about 9 AM yesterday morning, the tea boy knocked on the door to clean, and Chen replied from inside that he still needed to sleep, so the tea boy did not enter. He waited until noon and still did not see him get up, so he felt something was wrong. He pried the door open and saw that Chen was lying stiff on the bed. He touched him and found that he was already dead. The accountant then reported to the Fifth District First Precinct Public Concession, which sent police to investigate. A suicide note was found in the room, addressed to his wife, Xu Meixin, which read, "I am unable to support you, causing you to work day and night, yet we still struggle to make ends meet. It is better for me to end my life. You don't need to be sad. Our fate is over. It is okay for you to marry again." Below were the words "April 9th" and "Your weeping elder brother, Hongfu." The deceased's body was covered with bluish-purple congealed blood, suggesting that he had committed suicide by inhaling fumes. According to those who knew Chen Liang, Chen had borrowed three yuan from a friend, and his wife asked him the day before yesterday if he had returned it, which caused them to quarrel. Chen may have been overwhelmed with grief and felt the pressure of life, leading him to take this drastic measure.

Car Driver Still Trying to Evade Responsibility

Page 16

Li Pengsun sustained injuries and died soon after. At the time of the accident, the car driver did not sound the horn, resulting in the death. He has engaged lawyer Jiang Yiping to file a criminal complaint against Zhao, requesting that he be punished according to the law. Afterward, police officer No. 1865 arrived and ordered him to take the deceased to Tongren Hospital, where he died the next day. The court has verified that it was due to his own carelessness and not his fault. Lawyer Shen also stated that the police initially intended to file a public prosecution in this case. However, after the examination and investigation of the accident site, there was no evidence, so they did not prosecute. Judge Sun adjourned the hearing for seven days for further investigation.

Woman Sells Husband, Then He Dies 144

Woman Grieving and Driven Mad

Incoherent Speech, Utterly Miserable

Sent to Charity Organization for Care

Zhou Jin, a 34-year-old woman from Yuyao, Zhejiang, had been married to her husband, Zhou Jinmao, for over ten years. They had a nine-year-old daughter named A-mei. The couple came to Shanghai from their hometown in 1925 due to difficult living conditions. They resided in Caojiadu, Huxi. Her husband, Jinmao, worked as a laborer at the Zhentai Pier in the town, while she worked as a maid. The family of three was able to make a living temporarily. In recent years, prices have soared, and the cost of living has increased, leading to debt accumulation. In the autumn of last year, Jinmao was unable to repay his creditors and sold his daughter, A-mei, to someone. His wife loved her only daughter dearly and tried to stop him with all her might, but it was to no avail. She was grief-stricken by the loss of her daughter, and tears often wet her collar. She was filled with sorrow and despair. Jinmao also felt a sense of guilt and regret for having sold his daughter, as he was forced to do so. Soon after, he became seriously ill and bedridden. He eventually succumbed to his illness in November of last year. The woman was devastated by the loss of her beloved daughter and husband. Day after day, she grieved, which turned into depression, which then led to mental confusion and a nervous breakdown. She soon became mentally ill, eating irregularly and wandering aimlessly. Her madness was evident on the streets every day. Yesterday morning at about 1 AM, she was again acting madly in the Laobosheng Road area, babbling and crying miserably. A patrolling police officer noticed her and took her back to the Sixth District Police Station. After repeated questioning by District Chief Duan, she initially remained silent, only shedding tears. She then vaguely mentioned the above situation and said that she had worked as a helper at Mr. Zhang's office in the Dafeng Yarn Factory for a few months. However, she was incoherent about the rest and did not know her address. District Chief Duan believed that the madwoman had been stimulated and was pitiful. He prepared a document to send her to the Public Security Bureau for transfer to a charity organization for care.

Mother Died When She Was Four Months Old

Stepmother Abused Her and Forced Her to Marry

Raised by Her Aunt, Who Verbally Promised Her in Marriage

Wrote a Letter of Inquiry, But Entrusted the Wrong Person

Finally Achieved a Happy Ending After Many Hardships

The Woman's Family Background Ren Suzhen (nickname Mao Yuan), a 17-year-old woman from Ningbo, has a modern short haircut and is extremely beautiful. Her father, Ren Meifu, 56 years old, owns the Renshengji Watch Shop at the entrance of Huaqing Lane, East Tutang, Central Hongqiao, Xihuade Road. Suzhen's mother died when she was only four months old. Her aunt, Ms. Xin, from No. 140 Yipin Lane, Zhabei, raised her and sent her to school. Ji Caiyun, with whom she lived, had a son named Yifei, who was the same age as Suzhen and from the same hometown. Whenever they returned home from school, they would play together in the courtyard, like siblings. As a result, she was favored by Ms. Xin, who verbally promised her in marriage to Ji Yifei. Suzhen had long accepted this arrangement, but the engagement had not yet been formally arranged. In the spring of 1928, Yifei joined the postal service as a trainee, preventing the two from seeing each other morning and night. Ms. Xin, her aunt, passed away last winter, and Suzhen dropped out of school. This spring, she went to live with her father in Hongkou. However, her stepmother, Ms. Zhang, 37 years old,

Abused Her Regularly Recently, Ms. Zhang arranged for Suzhen to marry her sister's husband's younger brother (a car driver). Suzhen vowed not to comply, causing the mother and daughter to become like strangers. Yifei was depressed after leaving Suzhen. His parents learned the inside story and asked someone to propose marriage to the Ren family. However, the stepmother, Ms. Zhang, repeatedly refused, and the marriage was put on hold. Suzhen, living in an authoritarian family, spent her days in tears, repeatedly wanting to see Ji and pour out her heart. Chen Yonggen, a tailor who lived nearby, knew about the matter and offered to deliver letters. Suzhen then wrote a

Letter of Inquiry (original letter recorded below) on the 28th of last month and entrusted Chen's wife, A-ying, to deliver it. She soon received a reply stating, "I have received your letter. I hope you can come to the Fenghua Hotel on the 30th of this month to discuss everything," etc. Suzhen was overjoyed after receiving the letter. She went to the Fenghua Hotel with Chen's wife, A-ying, to wait. Ji did not arrive for a long time, and Ji's heart was full of doubt. She was afraid of being blamed by her stepmother if she went home. Just as she was in a dilemma, A-ying's younger brother suddenly drove a car to her residence, and she rode with him to stay at Eight Mile Bridge in Yangshupu for one day. The next morning, Chen Yonggen took Suzhen to Pudong to look for a friend. In the afternoon, they crossed the river again and stayed at the Nanyang Hotel on Minguo Road for one day. However, Suzhen refused to sleep, instead,

Waiting All Night Qin Qiusheng (21 years old, living in Tushanwan and doing advertising business), a friend of Chen, came and took her to the home of his relative, Qian Zusheng, who ran a grocery store in Tushanwan, to stay temporarily. On the day before yesterday (5th), Zhang Xiangrui, the patrol chief of the local police station, took her back to the Second Precinct of the Sixth District, believing that the woman's origins were unclear and her behavior suspicious. After a detailed interrogation by Chief Xu Yan, she confessed the above situation and said that she had been deceived this time. Fortunately, there was no coercion, and she was able to maintain her innocence, which was gratifying. However, she did not want to go home and asked the chief to

He also notified the Ren and Ji families to come to the station. Ji Yifei confessed that he was 17 years old, lived at No. 140 Yipin Lane, and was currently a trainee at the postal service. He knew nothing about the above situation. However, regarding the marriage, Ms. Xin had indeed agreed to it when she was alive. This spring, he had asked a matchmaker to propose marriage to the Ren family, but Ms. Zhang had demanded too much money for tea, so the marriage was called off. He pleaded with the chief to make a beautiful thing come true. Chief Xu learned the truth and sought the consent of both families, arranging for the marriage to be completed according to the original agreement that day. Suzhen was taken back by her maternal grandmother, Tang Yue, to await the Ji family's wedding. Qin Qiusheng and the other three detainees were released at the request of the woman's older sister, Ren Rongchang, and were not pursued further. After each signed a pledge, the love story of a woman seeking her husband came to an end.

Under the Supervision of the Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities 150

Business Conditions of the Xianghua Electric Company

There are many factories within the business area of the Xianghua Electric Company, so the electricity consumption has increased rapidly in recent years. The total revenue of the company in 1928 was more than 86,000 yuan, which increased to more than 123,000 yuan in 1929, an increase of about 47%. In terms of power generation projects, the Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities has repeatedly guided improvements, and fuel has been gradually saved. The average power generation in 1928 consumed 0.084 pounds of diesel per kilowatt-hour, which was reduced to 0.07 pounds in 1929. Fuel is a major expenditure for power plants. With fuel savings, expenses will naturally decrease. Therefore, the company's electricity revenue in 1929 increased by 47% compared with 1928, while expenses only increased by 34%. However, the Bureau of Public Utilities believes that small power plants generating electricity themselves are ultimately not as economical as purchasing electricity from large power plants for resale. Therefore, last autumn, the company was instructed to negotiate with the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company for power supply. Soon, the agreement was reached. Since January 1930, the company has stopped generating electricity and receives power from the Zhabei Company. From now on, Xianghua Company does not need to add machines, and the electricity supply can be expanded at any time. The work is simple, and expenses are reduced. According to the company's estimate, it can save more than 7,000 yuan per year. The business prospects are even more promising. As for Zhabei, it has one more large customer, and the business will inevitably improve greatly. Therefore, the Public Utilities Bureau's power supply plan is beneficial to both Zhabei and Xianghua, and its main purpose is to directly reduce power plant costs and indirectly reduce user burdens.

Son-in-Law is Deaf and Stupid

Daughter Unwilling to Marry

About six miles west of Sanlintang, Pudong, Pang Quanxing, the younger brother of Pang Zhenxing, a farmer from Pangjiaquan, 24th Bao, 2nd Tu, is 24 years old this year. Yesterday morning, presiding judge Guo Shouyi opened the sixth court for trial. Pang Zhenxing testified that he was 28 years old, from Shanghai, and lived in Pangjiaquan, Pudong. My younger brother Quanxing is 24 years old this year and currently works in ship repairing. He also stated the previous situation. The defendant Zhang Axiu testified that she was 24 years old and was deceived by the matchmaker in the past and hastily agreed to the marriage. Zhenxing replied, "My brother Quanxing is indeed deaf. He became deaf at the age of fifteen due to illness. He is out working today, so he did not come to court." Zhang Lu, 50 years old, testified, "Axiu is my daughter. She was deceived by the matchmaker in the past and only received 16 yuan in gifts, nothing else. It was not until last year that I learned that my son-in-law is deaf and stupid. Therefore, my daughter has repeatedly cried and quarreled with me to cancel the marriage. This kind of marriage, without her consent, she is unwilling to marry, and I have no way. Please investigate." The judge attempted to reconcile the parties in court, but they refused. Therefore, he invited Prosecutor Xu to present his opinion in court. The judge then announced the end of the debate and adjourned the hearing for judgment.

Student Carries Handgun Privately 154

Yesterday afternoon at about 5:00 PM, police officers Wang Chengwen and Yang Daocen from Post No. 3, Nanyang Bridge, Second District, Nanshi, along with inspectors Guo Zhenliang and Guo Chenghai, were inspecting pedestrians and passing vehicles near the iron shed entrance of Nanyang Bridge when they suddenly saw a white-licensed car (Shanghai 920, Concession 17530) driving from north to south. Several young men resembling students were sitting in the car. The police officers ordered the car to stop and searched each person. None of them had any prohibited items on their bodies. However, one of the teenagers looked flustered. They then ordered everyone to get out of the car and searched the car. They found a paper package containing a five-inch, five-peaked lotus-style revolver in the gap next to the seat on the left. There were no bullets. They asked the people if they had a gun license, and none of them did. They immediately took the car and everyone to the police station. After questioning each person one by one, District Chief Wang learned that the teenager carrying the gun was named Miao Wenquan, 19 years old, from Zhejiang. He is currently studying at the School of Commerce at Gordon Road, Public Concession. His father's name is Miao Zhixiang, who used to work at the Hanyang Arsenal in Hubei, serving as the director of the bullet manufacturing department. The gun was brought from Hubei to Shanghai in his early years and hidden at home. Later, he went out of town. He (Miao claimed) then took the gun to school to play with. A few days ago, his father suddenly returned home and learned that he had taken the gun to school. Fearing that it would cause trouble, his father ordered him to take it back immediately. This morning, his friends Tang Jinsheng, etc., came to school to play ball. In the afternoon, they went out together, so he took the gun along to take it back to his father's house in Lujiabang for storage. Unexpectedly, not long after leaving school, they encountered rain and hired a car at the Hengmao Car Company on Jing'an Temple Road. They were caught on Nanyang Bridge. The others confessed that their names were Tang Jinsheng, 20 years old, Tang Xianglin, 20 years old, Ren Mingjun, 22 years old, and Wu Zhihao, 21 years old, all locals. They all said that they were friends with Miao. This morning, they went to Miao's place to play. In the afternoon, when they left school, they saw Miao carrying a handgun. They all advised him not to carry it, but Miao did not listen. The others knew nothing about it. The driver, Yu Asi, 29 years old, from Yangzhou, confessed that they hired his car to go to Lujiabang, Nanshi, and he did not know they were carrying a handgun. After hearing the confessions, District Chief Wang immediately prepared a document and submitted it along with the car to the Judicial Section of the General Bureau for review.

Husband and Wife Separated for Eight Years 155

Suddenly Wants a Divorce After Cohabitation

Alimony of 2,000 Yuan

Paid in Four Installments

Li Yizhang, from Meixian, Guangdong, used to work in politics and is now unemployed in Shanghai, residing at his brother's house on Maigen Road. Li's brother used to be in the military and is now sighing about his situation, but he is still wealthy and does not worry about food and clothing. Yizhang is over thirty years old and originally married Ms. Tian Shenyi from Huaicheng. Tian came from a prominent family and studied from a young age. After marrying Li, because Li was ambitious and wanted to make his mark, Ms. Tian often stayed at her mother's house to focus on her studies, so Li would not have to worry about family matters. It has been eight years, and they still have no children. Last year, Li resigned from his position as secretary of a certain agency in Xiamen and came to Shanghai. Tian also came to Shanghai, hoping to enjoy the pleasures of family life from then on. Unexpectedly, this year, Li developed a lack of faith in his marriage with Tian and proposed a divorce. Tian also felt that Li was deeply addicted to gambling and did not provide for her, making it difficult to commit to a lifetime together. Therefore, she agreed to the proposed divorce, but proposed that she should be given a considerable amount of alimony to support her life. Li agreed to give 2,000 yuan, but stated that he would pay it when his finances were sufficient, and sent Tian a letter. This issue could have been resolved on its own, but for some reason, it still went through legal channels. Tian Shenyi appointed a lawyer and sued Li Yizhang in the Special District Local Court for abandonment and requested a divorce. Yesterday morning, Judge Yang opened a court session and summoned both parties and their lawyers. The divorce itself was not a point of contention between the two parties. The plaintiff, Tian Shenyi, argued that the defendant should provide alimony after the divorce. The amount was initially requested at 5,000 yuan, then reduced to 3,000 yuan. Finally, following the judge's advice, the defendant was ordered to pay 2,000 yuan. Li Yizhang repeatedly claimed poverty, saying that although he was willing to give 2,000 yuan at the time, he would have to wait until he found a job and then pay. He currently had no financial resources. If he made a promise rashly and could not pay at the time, he was afraid that he would be sued again. Judge Yang ordered him to pay the 2,000 yuan in four installments within one year, with one installment every three months, and each installment being 500 yuan. The first installment, as the plaintiff had an urgent need, was to be paid 200 yuan within two weeks, and 300 yuan after three months, with the rest paid in installments. This would be easier to do, and Li finally agreed. Thus, the case was settled through reconciliation.

Special Article

Xu Peikun's Gold is Expensive, Silver is Cheap Relief Plan (Continued) 162

(5) The Power of Shanghai Gold Speculators

In addition to domestic conditions, international payments, and East exchange rate reasons, there is another important comparable force, which is gold speculation. The Shanghai gold price can fluctuate depending on the East exchange rate, London silver bullion, or other reasons, but sometimes its fluctuations are completely unaffected by any overseas market and are absolutely based on China's domestic conditions and the psychology of domestic speculators. The changes in the gold price in the second month of the lunar calendar were of this type. In addition, cross rates between the British and Japanese currencies and between the Japanese and American currencies also have considerable influence on the changes in the gold price. However, it is also the case for the Shanghai silver exchange rate. In other words, speculators make their gold transactions based on the above-mentioned cross rates.

(6) Reasons for Recent Changes in Silver Exchange Rates

At this point, we can examine the forces controlling the Shanghai silver exchange rate. Since the beginning of the exchange rate turmoil in February, the gold price and the silver exchange rate behind it have fluctuated abnormally. First, there were various rumors such as the imposition of taxes on the import of silver bullion by India and the United States, and the dumping of unusable currency accepted by India and Annam. Afterwards, there was the actual implementation of the policy of dealing with silver bullion by governments of various overseas countries. All of these are related to the destruction of the local gold market. Recently, rumors of restrictions on the import of silver bullion by the Chinese government have also affected the gold market. This phenomenon can only be explained by the principle of speculation, and there is no other principle that can be understood.

(7) Invention of the Complex Principle of Silver Exchange Rate Plunge

In summary, the Shanghai silver exchange rate is affected by international payments, East exchange rate, gold speculation, London silver bullion prices, and many other intangible forces. Among these forces, except for international payments, the rest can be included in the item of speculation. In principle, the Shanghai silver exchange rate is restricted by the international payments principle and the speculation principle. However, because the latter's influence has been particularly significant recently, this exchange rate phenomenon can be purely explained by the latter alone. The author firmly believes that other reasons are all useless and easily lead to incorrect results. Furthermore, this complex speculation principle is applicable not only to the past and present, but also to the future before China's financial system is reformed.

(D) Relief Plans Amidst the Cry for Help

The gold standard issue is clearly the cause of the changes in the Shanghai silver exchange rate, so it is no longer difficult to devise a remedy. Many commentators vaguely say that the gold standard system is sufficient to remedy all difficulties, but the author does not believe that this strategy can relieve the current difficulties, and believes that it will intensify the current turmoil.

(1) The Gold Standard Issue

In principle, there is no doubt that China's currency system should be thoroughly reorganized. However, the implementation of the gold standard policy is not yet the time. The people of the country are now extremely poor and cannot withstand the suffering and sacrifice during the transitional period of reform. Adopting the gold standard system in a country with unclear politics and backward economy will inevitably make the current situation even more chaotic and cause violent expansion and contraction of the new currency system at home and abroad. Argentina, Brazil, Chile, Peru, and other South American countries have all experienced this situation. Even in the European war and the post-war experiences of the United Kingdom, France, Germany, and Russia, it is clear that the exchange rate parity between gold-using countries can be disrupted. The Japanese gold after the 1923 earthquake gave us a lesson in complex exchange rate phenomena. In short, it is absurd to insist on a gold standard policy before our country is fully prepared to deal with all difficulties. As for the gold standard system as a currency policy, it should be discussed separately. (To be continued)

Dismissed with a Laugh, by a Wanderer

Child (a neighbor gives him a piece of bread): Madam, thank you.

Neighbor: You're welcome. But I really like it when children know manners. I really like hearing him say "Thank you."

Child: Madam, if you like to hear me say "Thank you" again, then put more jam on this bread for me.

Philanthropist ("visiting a prison"): What crime did you commit to come to this prison?

Criminal: For borrowing money.

Philanthropist: Borrowing money from someone isn't a crime. How did you end up here?

Criminal: Because that person wouldn't lend me the money. I cracked his head open.

Young man (meeting his lover's mother for the first time): Auntie, your kind face looks very familiar. It seems like I've met you somewhere before.

Lover's mother: Yes, I was buying things on the main street the day before yesterday, carrying many big and small bags on the tram. I stood in front of you for more than half an hour, but you pretended to read a book and never offered me a seat.

Unemployed person: I'm good at performing. I can be a walking advertisement.

Casual Chat About Chrysanthemums by Zheng Yimei 163

My neighbor, Hua Jingyun, is a theater enthusiast. He often associates with actors and is familiar with inside stories. Yesterday, he told me about Wang Xiaonong and Tan Jinpei. I am recording it on the left as material for this column. Wang Xiaonong was a scholar who lived as an actor. He excelled in literary talent. His poems, such as his self-composed verse on the Peach Blossom Fan, "Elegance is ceded to Yang Longyou, the peach blossoms are painted on the fan. But it's Yun Ting who collects it, now I leap onto the stage." It has been widely spread in artistic circles. Xiaonong once kept a myna bird in his residence. Xiaonong practiced singing songs, and the myna bird could imitate him. In the play "The Party Members' Monument," it could even use its tone and modulate the melody, moving and inspiring people. Compared with Sima Xiangru's parrot reciting the "Ode to Master Grand," it was not much inferior. Xiaonong loved it very much. One day, it was hanging in a cage in front of the eaves when it was suddenly clawed by a neighbor's cat. Because Xiaonong was protecting the myna bird, he moved away to avoid it. However, after being injured, the myna bird gradually stopped eating and died after a few days. Xiaonong was depressed and unhappy for months. His peers all considered him foolish.

The king of the acting world, Tan Xinpei, had an opium addiction. He would lie on a couch in his residence every day, enjoying the pleasure of exhaling smoke. After exhaling, he would get up in the room to practice his songs. This was to prepare for performing on stage in the evening. The four walls of the room were inlaid with sparkling mirrors. The king practiced singing, paying attention to his appearance. Every wave of his sleeve, every stamp of his foot, he had to do it in front of the mirror. Only when it was appropriate and satisfying would he stop. His dedication to practice was extraordinary. This is why the king is the king.

Treasures Awaiting Unearthing: The Precarious Situation in Northeast China

The Melon-Fighting Festival in Persia is Grand 164

Persia is also an ancient country in the East. It borders the Red Sea and is adjacent to Arabia. To this day, it has not completely shed the customs of nomadic peoples.

Their custom of "melon fighting" is extremely interesting. Every year after the autumn harvest, melon-fighting festivals are held, large ones in cities and small ones in villages, all with organized melon-fighting associations for entertainment. However, it also contains a slight gambling element, similar to horse racing in Europe and America. Before the melon-fighting begins, the organizers choose a suitable location and date and announce it to the public. At the opening of the event, a table is placed in the center of the field. A melon is placed on the table, and people place bets, limited to red or white pulp. Those who guess correctly win a large prize, otherwise they simply shout in disappointment. After everyone has placed their bets, the organizers use a knife to cut open the melon to show the color of the pulp.

In the eyes of Persians, this is a traditional form of entertainment. Some people have become rich because of it, and many have been ruined by it. The matter is entertainment but close to gambling. It is said that the Persian government is planning to ban it.

This time, the Zhejiang immigrants going to the Northeast have set a precedent for opening up wasteland and colonizing the borders for the southeastern provinces. The first batch of 315 people has already set off on the Huayang Wheel. Mr. Hu Ruyin, one of the transportation staff, has been in the Northeast for more than 20 years, handling railway and civil engineering projects. The Zhejiang government requested him to go along, truly for the sake of the immigrants' happiness. According to Mr. Hu, the richness of natural resources in the Northeast and the intensity of a certain country's invasion are alarming. I will briefly record one or two of them below:

300 Yuan Turns into 400,000 Mr. Hu said that he knew a certain Lu person in the Eastern Province who brought 300 yuan to Fengtian (Mukden). Now he has 400,000 yuan and has become a wealthy man. Three brothers could not survive in their home province, so they sold their property and houses and gathered 300 yuan to go out to the pass. They used 200 yuan for a year's food and 100 yuan to lease a piece of land (land in the Eastern Province is measured in "fang," each "fang" being 480 mu). Using three donkeys and horses, the three brothers personally cultivated the land. After a year, it became productive land. Each mu of farmland was worth 20 yuan. Then he used the cultivated land to mortgage for 2,000 yuan from a large landlord and continued to lease 20 "fang." Continuing to cultivate one "fang" and mortgage it for several "fang." By last year, the three brothers had been out of the pass for ten years. After checking their assets, they had reached more than 400,000 yuan. Now they have divided it into three shares and are clearly three wealthy men.

The Xing'an Mountains are Full of Gold The Xing'an Mountains in the Eastern Province are a gold mining area in China. The Liaoning authorities have sent Zou Zuohua to develop it. Mr. Hu, who specializes in civil engineering, said that he personally went to the sandy areas of the Xing'an Mountains for a field survey. Panning the sand revealed a lot of red gold. Local indigenous people also pan for gold there, but the refining method is outdated. The labor is huge, and the gold obtained is meager. If a huge investment can be made to set up new gold panning machines, then gold will be everywhere, inexhaustible. Governor Zou is already planning it.

Natural Alkali Blocks Can Be Picked Up Everywhere Shanghai's Brunner Mond & Co. sells alkali to our country, worth millions of dollars every year. But the alkali in the Three Eastern Provinces is as abundant as dung, everywhere. The residents there do not engage in agricultural work. They go to the alkali-producing areas every day to pick up these natural alkali blocks. Each child can pick up 2,000 cash, and adults can pick up 3,000 cash. This has fostered the laziness of these people. Recently, Britain and Japan are vying to buy it cheaply, but the Chinese people do not know about this product.

The Astonishing Output of Miscellaneous Grains The South Manchurian Railway only occupies the land of three counties. The entire line is only 200 kilometers long. Mr. Hu, who has worked on the railway for a long time, said that the railway's business relies entirely on transporting soybeans, millet, and sorghum. The freight is extremely cheap, but it can collect 6 million yuan in transportation fees every year. The huge amount of miscellaneous grains produced in these three counties is truly astonishing. However, 50% to 60% has not yet been developed and planted. The Income of the South Manchurian Railway is Frightening The daily income of the South Manchurian Railway has now reached 380,000 yuan. One month is 11.4 million yuan, and one year can collect 136.8 million yuan. Of this money, more than 90% comes from the Chinese people. The money leaked out over the years is unknown. Schools are also established along the way, specializing in enrolling Chinese students under the age of fifteen. Tuition is free. Chinese people who are fooled by their greed and profit send their children in. But they are taught Japanese. After graduation, they forget their ancestors and ancestors. It is no different from creating countless Japanese-influenced Chinese who invade China for the Japanese. Their plan is even more alarming.

A Strange and Respectable Abducted Child Shi Long 165

Last winter, Huajiaqiao Town, southeast of Kunshan, suddenly suffered a bandit robbery. In the end, several people were abducted, including three members of Hu Xinchen's family: Xinchen's sister-in-law, Xinchen's son, and Xinchen's grandson. The grandson was only ten years old. After being abducted, Xinchen's son falsely claimed to be a partner, not a Hu family member. He was lucky enough to be released halfway. This ten-year-old grandson was first put on a boat. Then he saw his father being abducted as well. If it were any other child, he would have cried out for his father. But this child acted as if he had nothing to do with him. He didn't cry or call out to his father. This is also strange. When Xinchen's son falsely claimed to be a partner and was released alone, if it were any other child, he would have cried out again. But this child looked at it as if he didn't see anything. If he had revealed any trace, Xinchen's son would not have been able to return. This was described in detail by the people of Huajiaqiao, who also said that this child was usually exceptionally intelligent. His ability to endure, not crying or calling out, was intended to protect his father. And his father was indeed saved. It can be said that he was filial. It is said that Xinchen's sister-in-law has also been released. Only this strange and respectable ten-year-old child, because the ransom was too high, could not be redeemed for a while. Now the bandits are being suppressed, their traces scattered, and there is no news. Xinchen and his son are weeping all day long, thinking of this good child. It is also pitiful.

Recording the Story of a Beggar Woman Who Became Rich Huang Yingdai 166

There are many ways to get rich. But I have never heard of getting rich by begging. Surprisingly, our Song (Songjiang) has a beggar woman who became rich by begging. The matter is bizarre, so I will briefly describe the circumstances of her getting rich on the left:

A certain beggar woman, her name is unknown, is from Song. She is already over sixty years old. Her family is extremely poor. She became a widow early, and her son is unfilial. Unable to make a living, she begged for a living. She must wait by the Malu Bridge every day, begging to passersby. Malu Bridge is the pier for Songjiang paddle boats, and it is also the only way to take a bus to the West Railway Station. Therefore, there is a lot of traffic to and fro. When a guest passes over Malu Bridge, the woman must follow him, unleashing her torrent of words, begging him until he reaches into his pocket and then leaves. I recall that when we were studying abroad, every time we returned to Song, we would see the woman begging people by Malu Bridge. The woman is quite stingy. She lives very frugally. Every day, what she gets from begging, besides buying steamed buns and vegetarian noodles to fill her stomach, she must gather and save the remaining money. At first, the woman did not know that begging could also lead to wealth. But money, as a thing, can accumulate little by little. And after the woman's savings reached one silver dollar, she would lend it to others, earning one dime of interest per month, which could earn one yuan and two dimes per year. The child is more than the mother, which is the so-called "loan sharking." Through such exploitation, in a few years, the woman had several hundred silver dollars in her hands. But the business of begging, the woman has never abandoned it. Over time, the more money she accumulated, the more people from all walks of life and wandering wanderers, when they were in need, would borrow from her. And the woman would always respond. For a time, the people of Song all knew that the woman had money. It became a beautiful story spread in the streets and alleys. In addition to lending money, the woman also used the remaining money to buy funeral clothes and funeral items for her afterlife. But her son was one of the unemployed vagrants. When he could not make ends meet, he would sneak into the house and secretly steal the woman's money and funeral clothes. When the woman discovered it, she would wail to the sky. Her appearance was quite sad. This happened several times. But the woman could not do anything about it. And because of her deep love for her son, she did not want him to go to jail. Now, there is no trace of the woman by Malu Bridge. Whether she is alive or not is unknown.

Yarn, Cotton, and Silk Markets Are Increasingly Weak 174

The yarn market remains flat and weak, with no distinction between gains and losses. This stalemate seems to have the potential to last for a long time. Therefore, transactions are sluggish, and both bulls and bears maintain firm stances. However, most retail investors are bearish because the peak season for temporary workers is approaching. The situation is unstable, and overseas cotton yarn market conditions are also softening. Although manufacturers are holding on tightly, some are watching for imported yarns costing 50 taels. According to customs reports, cotton yarn exports last month were relatively brisk, totaling over 80,000 bales. The yarn market is currently being hit by the war, making it difficult to achieve significant development.

There are many short-selling positions in forward contracts.
