Grain and Rice Prices are High and Flat, with Secondary Declining 178

Secondary-Grade Cargo Ships Return to Western Roads for Sale

Yesterday, the source of cargo entering the Zhabei district via Guo Lu was not strong. Sales on this street remained slow. River stocks have not decreased. Therefore, the cargo ships carrying secondary-grade goods have been waiting for a long time. If there are no more customers, it is feared that there will be losses. As a result, more than a dozen ships have returned to sell their goods on the western roads. The price of this returned cargo is about 17.5 yuan. Therefore, the wholesale price of white japonica rice has gradually stabilized, but transactions remain scarce. The source of thin indica rice is seen to be scarce, and sales are slow. The price lacks fluctuations. The price of Yangjian rice remains sluggish. The demand for Dujian rice at various stalls is extremely flat, and prices are barely holding up. The Tongbian customer base selects high-quality goods and makes cautious purchases. The supply of Yinyuan goods is scarce, and prices have not risen or fallen.

About ten cargo ships arrived at the South Shanghai river wharves, but sales were not very brisk. Changshu-Wuxi top-grade japonica rice was flat, while ordinary rice saw a slight drop in wholesale prices. Stores were not greedy for Su-Tong machine-milled japonica rice and only had sporadic transactions. Market prices were similar to the previous day. The price of thin early indica rice from Southern provinces remained firm as there were no eager buyers from Ningbo, and the supply was scarce. Therefore, there were no price reductions. The demand for Yang-Du pointed rice remained quiet because cargo owners were in no rush to sell, and there were no profits or losses. Sales of White Yuan rice were average, and buyers were hesitant to pay high prices for Diaopi (coarsely milled rice). The market was weak.

Near-Term Flour Prices Expected to Exceed 5 Qian 179

Yesterday, the flour market was stable. In the morning, there was still some activity from Tianjin brokers, but in the afternoon, they became more cautious. Therefore, the situation was slightly eased. However, the stocks of spot goods at Fuxin were extremely thin due to direct shipments to Tianjin and procurement for Tianjin brokers. Therefore, even small transactions on this street could not be purchased and shipped immediately. Therefore, the attitude of the factory was to still see prices above 5 qian in the current month. They seem unwilling to relax if the price does not reach this level. As for the distant months, market sentiment turned flat as the quoted price of imported wheat slightly returned by 0.457 jiao. However, if the current month's prices are raised again, the June contract must be brought up. Although new wheat may be seen in June, it is said that factory sales and purchases can only be made in mid-June. Therefore, there may still be problems ahead. As a result, the current month was 0.005 yuan higher than the previous day. The June to September contracts remained unchanged, and the October contract was 0.0025 yuan higher.

Wheat Futures Hovering with a Tightening Trend 180

Spot Prices Also Call for 0.05 or 0.06 Yuan Higher

Yesterday, over 11,000 bags were traded.

Yesterday, the wheat futures market showed a stable trend. Although the quoted price of imported wheat repeatedly fell back, domestic wheat farmers still thought of holding firm before the new wheat was harvested. The new short sellers in the producing areas had to be wary of the influence of the Suzhou broker group. Therefore, the market hovered with a tightening trend throughout the day, and the inability to maintain prolonged sunny weather seemed to be a guarantee for the bulls to hold on to their positions. As a result, the June and July contracts were 0.01 yuan higher than the previous day, the August and September contracts remained unchanged, and the October contract was slightly down by 0.01 yuan in the morning but did not trade in the afternoon. After the surge in spot wheat prices this month, the quoted prices in various producing areas also rose, and factories actively bought even several points higher due to the active flour sales. Yesterday, the asking price for high-quality wheat was 0.05 or 0.06 yuan higher than the previous day. Thick Biequ fabric and French flannel have smooth sales trends 182

Thick Biequ fabric is mostly used for Western suits, with strong sales in the summer. Fabrics with silk-like stripes and crepe-like gray-yellow colors are sought after by woolen fabric stores. Wholesale prices are around 0.3 taels per yard, while retail prices are 6-7 yuan. Slightly lower-grade fabrics sell for 0.22-0.23 taels. Those with a soft and glossy texture must be priced above 0.34-0.35 taels, which are known in the market as fashionable Balle fabrics. Lower-grade fabrics with stripes and solid colors from brands such as Tianyou, Hao Shi, Rongtai, Anli, and Hualun sell for only 0.18-0.19 taels per yard.

The sales season for French flannel is longer than that of thick Biequ fabric, with the strongest sales in the spring and autumn seasons. Colors are divided into yellow, white, gray, blue, striped, plaid, solid colors, etc. The most popular colors in the market recently are blue and white-gray. Prices range from 0.2 taels to 0.34-0.35 taels per yard. The lower-grade fabrics selling for around 0.2 taels last week have now sold out. There are also few stocks left of the 0.24-0.25 tael fabrics. Yesterday, those holding the goods raised prices, and stores had no choice but to increase their purchase prices accordingly. Therefore, brands such as Zhongzheng, Ningfeng, Hongsheng, Gongyi, and Gongping are generally unwilling to sell at low prices.

Oil Market Tung Oil Prices Loosen and Fall 184

The peak sales season for refined tung oil is in the autumn. Sales are not weak in the spring and summer seasons, but they are not as strong as in the new autumn. At the beginning of this year's spring, the price of top-grade refined tung oil was still above 0.3 taels. Later, due to the loosening of the prices of Hong oil and Bai oil, tung oil was inevitably affected, so it fell to 0.3 taels. However, the various oil presses in the producing areas carefully studied the oil color, and the cost was high. They were unwilling to follow the price drop of Hong oil and Bai oil, so the new cargo remained very firm. They were willing to keep it for a long time. Currently, it is between the spring and summer sales seasons, just in a sluggish period. Therefore, the local oil and hemp shops temporarily reduced prices in order to stimulate buyers' interest, waiting for the summer sales to slightly increase before raising prices again. Therefore, the top-grade Wanxing, Yu Da Youheng, and other brands were all dropped by 0.1 tael, and others by several qian. However, this is not due to weakness in the market, so it is expected that prices will increase again soon.

Recently, the troupe's core members have reorganized, including veterans Xu Tiansheng, Jin Xinmin, Liang Enyan, Gan Huanting, Chen Zhaofang, Wang Qianxia, and Feng Yanxia. They have scheduled to hold the first preparatory joint meeting this Sunday morning at the Guanshengyuan on Nanjing Road to discuss the direction of progress.

Dance Hall News 190

The Oriental Dance Research Association at No. 431, Yixin Lane, Laoyao Road, announces that the association has been in operation for four years without interruption. More than 4,000 members have graduated, and its reputation is outstanding. Recently, the association has received letters from all walks of life requesting the addition of an external teaching course to facilitate those who are busy with work and the ladies of the boudoir to enjoy the benefits of learning to dance. Since the addition of this course, invitations from all walks of life to teach at home have been pouring in, indicating its popularity.

Calligraphy and Painting News 191

The Honeybee Painting Society Fan Exhibition announces that the society's fan exhibition is scheduled for twenty days, with replacements every five days. The first replacement period has arrived, and the works on display are even better than the previous ones. If art enthusiasts are willing to visit, the society extends its warmest welcome.

Publishing News 192

In order to develop foreign trade, enhance international credit, and guide the improvement of domestic goods, the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau has published the "International Trade Herald." The first issue has already been published and sold widely. The second issue was published on the first of this month. The contents include the bureau's work report at the Commodity Inspection Conference, a history of the Chinese tea trade, an overview of the Chinese cotton trade, an overview of the Shanghai tea industry, a study on the disinfection of raw cowhide, chemical inspection methods for egg products, the production status and geographical distribution of Chinese cotton, an overview of Japanese investment in China, and various statistics on wool and tea production in various countries around the world and silk exports in recent decades. All of these are carefully written by experts and are of great value. Each issue costs 30 cents, half a year is $1.60, and a full year is $3.00. Subscriptions can be arranged with the Bureau's Office at No. 15 Museum Road. Beixin, Qixin, Kaiming, Guanghua, and other bookstores also sell it on consignment. The third issue is already being compiled and includes "Observing Our Country's National Economy from Import and Export Trade" by Dr. Shou Jingwei and "An Overview of the Shanghai Silk Factory Industry" by silk expert Miao Zhongxiu.

Wireless Transmission of Newspapers Successfully Achieved for the First Time 193

The San Francisco Call-Bulletin, published in San Francisco, transmitted its full front page via wireless to Schenectady, New York, in late March on the 21st. This marks the beginning of the wireless transmission of original newspaper text. San Francisco and Schenectady are 2,500 miles apart, and the transmission was completely successful. It is anticipated that the front pages of the London Times or the New York Times will soon be transmitted to Nanjing or Shanghai. According to the American magazine "Editor & Publisher," regarding the Call-Bulletin's transmission, three hours after the newspaper was published on March 21st, people in the research laboratory of the General Electric Company in Schenectady were able to read the full page of its front page. The page was transmitted via wireless, traveling 2,500 miles through space. In the laboratory, it was completely copied to its original size by a new automatic copying machine. Wireless technicians claim this is the first successful attempt of this kind. It is predicted that eventually, wireless will be able to transmit most commercial mail and deliver daily newspapers to readers' homes daily. Furthermore, according to a statement issued by the General Electric Company, several years ago, the company's chairman, Owen Young (the author of the Young Plan), gave a speech at a banquet honoring the new president of the Radio Corporation of America, Harbord, stating that he hoped to one day see the front page of the London Times transmitted electronically in New York City. This transmission has somewhat fulfilled Young's prediction. The new machine for copying the newspaper page was developed by Charles Young, Owen Young's son. The machine is the size of an ordinary small suitcase and can be connected to any wireless receiver, like a speaker. The text it receives is printed on a roll of paper, which moves through the machine at a rate of about one and a half inches per minute. In this test, for convenience, a shortwave receiver was used, and the paper was 8 inches wide. The full front page of the Call-Bulletin was printed on three sheets of paper. However, technicians say that the width of the paper is probably not limited to 8 inches because the machine is still under development. The transmitter in San Francisco was built by Dr. Alexanderson in the research laboratory of the General Electric Company and installed at the company's shortwave radio station in Oakland, California, broadcasting using a 17.3-meter wavelength. Dr. Alexanderson, Young, and the technicians are unwilling to discuss the details of the transmission and the copying machine, only saying that the results are interesting, but much development is still needed to complete it.

The Story of World Literature (1) (4) (9) by John Macy, translated by Hu Zhongchi 194

Chapter 38: French Prose of the 19th Century

Seeing and singing of good and evil,

He now controls the singing keys of all.

– Swinburne, "Victor Hugo"

As I tried to say while narrating the English lyric poets of the seventeenth century, the schools or types of poetry are so intertwined that they confuse those who try to draw definite lines. We cannot say where school A ends and school B begins. Nineteenth-century (and the years before and after) French poetry is indistinctly divided into these three groups: Romantic, Parnassian, and Symbolist. In both English and French Romanticism (the movements in both countries are inexplicably similar and yet different), in both form and content, broke free from the shackles of tradition, sought material in the past, in the depths of their own souls, and in the stars, loosening Pegasus's reins. The Parnassians, on the other hand, resisted the indulgence of the Romantics, their personal laments, and Byronian egoism, striving to make poetry objective, impersonal, "inhuman," not as cold as marble, but as pure, solid, and clear as a beautiful statue. This was a new classicism that even considered Shakespeare and Dante "vulgar." Next came the Symbolists, who advocated the necessity of personal things, the singing of oneself, and claimed that doing anything else honestly was impossible. Their critical spokesperson, Edmond de Goncourt, said that the only justification for writing is to express one's own personality. These three schools and several subordinate factions (it is said that France has a new school of poetry every fifteen years) are not fundamentally hostile or conflicting, because after all, poetry is always poetry. Leconte de Lisle, the greatest figure of the Parnassians, was just as personal in his own way as Verlaine was in his. The Parnassians spoke of and practiced the beauty of form and the beauty of sound. Verlaine's greatest slogan was, "Music above all else." The Symbolists, who expressed their moods and sentiments, conveying their emotions and feelings to the reader through suggestion, certainly had little to argue with the early Romantics. For example, didn't Lamartine do the same in "The Lake" and "In Solitude"? If it is said that the Parnassians have some similarities with the realists in novels, then where is the line between Romanticism and Realism? This old question arises again. However, as for modern poets, we will not fully understand them if we try to determine which chair they sit on in the school.

The French Romantic movement in poetry, to the extent that a definite beginning can be pointed out, began with André Chénier, the amazing young poet who died on the scaffold at the age of thirty-two. He drew his inspiration from Greek and Latin. Although the Romantics called him a precursor, he was truly a thorough classicist. However, his classicism was not pedantic. It was not something borrowed or consciously studied, but a part of his nature, a true classicism. His poetry was soft and beautiful, so the Romantics called him father. Some of his poems, if included in a Greek anthology, would be quite appropriate.

The great ballad poet and popular songwriter Béranger, although his vigorous songs were certainly not incompatible with his admiring Romantic contemporaries, did not belong to the Romantic group but was entirely isolated. His songs or ballads were dazzling, colorful, and skillfully varied. The vocabulary was simple and honest, and the rhythm, even if not subtle, was singable. In that category, though not the greatest, it was complete. There was no ballad like the one pointing at Napoleon that was so full of soaring spirit.

Once there was a king of Yvetot,

The first great poet in the Romantic group was Lamartine. His "Meditations," which were never surpassed by his later works, is one of the defining books in French literature. Such melody had not been heard in France since the seventeenth century. It was something spontaneous, fresh, and pure, a sorrow, a gentle sorrow bordering on sentimentality. The mood of "Twilight and Memory" was completely honest. The scope of his emotions was limited, and his delicate colors almost faded to invisibility before the magnificent brilliance of Hugo and his school. However, later poets and critics looked at him with increasing admiration. There is no doubt about this. His most famous poem is "The Lake," from which I will quote two verses translated by Shelley:
